Topic: Math
Question: The difference between the squares of two numbers is 256000 and the sum of the numbers is 1000. The numbers are
Choices:
  A: 600, 400
  B: 628, 372
  C: 640, 360
  D: None of these
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let x and y be the two numbers. 
  We have two equations:
    x^2 - y^2 = 256000
    x + y = 1000
  We can use algebra to solve for x and y.

Solution:
  x^2 - y^2 = (x+y)(x-y) = 256000
  x + y = 1000
  From the first equation, we know that (x+y)(x-y) = 256000
  Substituting x+y = 1000, we get (1000)(x-y) = 256000
  Solving for x-y, we get x-y = 256
  Adding x+y = 1000 and x-y = 256, we get 2x = 1256, so x = 628
  Substituting x = 628 into x+y = 1000, we get y = 372

  Therefore, the two numbers are 628 and 372.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the two numbers are x and y.
  The difference between the squares of two numbers can be represented as (x^2 - y^2) = (x + y)(x - y).
  The sum of the numbers is x + y = 1000.
  
Calculation:
  (x + y)(x - y) = 256000
  x + y = 1000
  
  Let's solve for x - y:
  (x + y)(x - y) = 256000
  (1000)(x - y) = 256000
  x - y = 256
  
  We now have two equations with two variables:
  x + y = 1000
  x - y = 256
  
  Solving for x and y:
  x = (1000 + 256)/2 = 628
  y = (1000 - 256)/2 = 372
  
  Therefore, the numbers are 628 and 372.

  Since x > y, the numbers are 628 and 372.

Topic: Math
Question: A company produces 420 units of a particular computer component every month, at a production cost to the company of $110 per component, and sells all of the components by the end of each month. What is the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee that the yearly profit (revenue from sales minus production costs) will be at least $626,400 ?
Choices:
  A: 226
  B: 230
  C: 240
  D: 260
  E: 280
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The company produces 420 units of a particular computer component every month.
  The production cost to the company of each component is $110.
  The yearly profit (revenue from sales minus production costs) should be at least $626,400.
  
Calculation:
  The yearly production cost is: 420 * 12 * $110 = $554,400.
  The yearly revenue should be: $554,400 + $626,400 = $1,180,800.
  The minimum selling price per component should be: $1,180,800 / (420 * 12) = $230.
  
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The company produces 420 units of a particular computer component every month.
  The production cost to the company of each component is $110.
  The yearly profit (revenue from sales minus production costs) should be at least $626,400.

  The yearly revenue from sales should be: $626,400 + $554,400 = $1,180,800/year
  The minimum selling price per component can be calculated as follows:
  Minimum Selling Price = (Yearly Revenue from Sales) / (Total Units Produced per Year)
  Minimum Selling Price = $1,180,800 / (420 units/month x 12 months/year) = $230/unit

  5040(x - 110) >= 626400
  x - 110 >= 124
  x >= 234
  The minimum selling price per component that will guarantee a yearly profit of at least $626,400 is $240. Therefore, the answer is C.

Knowledge: To solve this problem, we can use the Pythagorean theorem, which states that in a right triangle, the square of the length of the hypotenuse (the side opposite the right angle) is equal to the sum of the squares of the lengths of the other two sides.

Action: Answer("C")

sqrt((5 km)^2 + (3 km)^2) = sqrt(25 km^2 + 9 km^2) = sqrt(34 km^2)  5.83 km

Therefore, A is approximately 4 km from home.

  (a + b)2 = a2 + 2ab + b2
  (a - b)2 = a2 - 2ab + b2

6a2b2 - 6ab3 = b2(a2 + 2ab + b2)
Dividing both sides by 6b:
(a2 - ab - b2)/(a + b)2 = 1/6

6a2 - 6ab - 6b2 = a2 + 2ab + b2
5a2 - 8ab + 5b2 = 0
(a - b)(5a - 5b) = 0

Therefore, a = b or 5a = 5b, which means that (a + b) cannot be equal to zero, so we can eliminate option A.

Option B is the same as the right-hand side of the equation, so it cannot be the answer.

Option D is not related to the equation, so we can eliminate it.

Option E is not a valid answer, so we can eliminate it.

Question: Everyone in the family earns money each month. If the total income of a family per month is $9000 and the median income is $3000, how many members are there in the family?

  A: 2
  B: 3

  The median is the middle value of a set of numbers.

  If the total income of the family is $9000, and the median income is $3000, then there must be an odd number of family members.
  The sum of the incomes of all family members divided by the number of family members will give the average income per family member.

Calculation:
  If the median income is $3000, then there are an equal number of family members earning less than $3000 and more than $3000.
  So, the total income earned by family members earning less than $3000 is equal to the total income earned by family members earning more than $3000.
  Let's assume that there are 'n' family members.
  Then, the total income earned by family members earning less than $3000 is earned by (n-1)/2 family members.
  And, the total income earned by family members earning more than $3000 is earned by (n-1)/2 family members.
  So, the total income earned by family members earning less than $3000 is (n-1)/2 * $3000 = $1500(n-1).
  And, the total income earned by family members earning more than $3000 is (n-1)/2 * $3000 = $1500(n-1).
  The total income earned by the family is $9000.
  So, $1500(n-1) + $1500(n-1) = $9000
  $3000(n-1) = $9000
  n-1 = 3
  n = 4

  Therefore, there are 3 family members in the family. Answer: (B)

  The total income divided by the number of family members will give us the average income.
  If the median income is $3000, it means that there are family members who earn more than $3000 and family members who earn less than $3000.
  The sum of all the family members' income divided by the number of family members will give us the average income.
  We can use the median income and the total income to find out how many family members there are.

Calculation:
  If the median income is $3000, then there are family members who earn more than $3000 and family members who earn less than $3000.
  Let's assume that there are x family members who earn less than $3000 and y family members who earn more than $3000.
  Then, we can write the following equation:
  x + y = total number of family members
  The median income is $3000, which means that there are (x + y) / 2 family members who earn less than $3000 and (x + y) / 2 family members who earn more than $3000.
  The total income of the family is $9000, which means that:
  x * 3000 + y * 3000 = 9000
  3000 * (x + y) = 9000
  x + y = 3
  We can substitute this value in the equation x + y = total number of family members:
  3 = total number of family members

Topic: Math
Question: A starts a business with Rs.40,000. After 2 months, B joined him with Rs.60,000. C joined them after some more time with Rs.120,000. At the end of the year, out of a total profit of Rs.375,000, C gets Rs.150,000 as his share. How many months after B joined the business, did C join?
Choices:
  A: 2 months
  B: 4 months
  C: 23 months
  D: 24 months
  E: 84 months
Response 0:
Let's find the share of A and B first, and then we can find the time when C joined.
Total investment = Rs. 40,000 (A) + Rs. 60,000 (B) = Rs. 100,000
Let's assume C joined after x months.
So, C's investment = Rs. 120,000 and time period = (12 - x) months
Total profit = Rs. 375,000
C's share = Rs. 150,000
Therefore, A and B's share = Total profit - C's share = Rs. 375,000 - Rs. 150,000 = Rs. 225,000
Now, we can find the ratio of their profits:
A : B : C = (40,000 x 12) : (60,000 x 10) : (120,000 x (12 - x))
A : B : C = 4 : 3 : 9 - 3x
We know that C's share is Rs. 150,000, so we can write:
9x/(9-3x) * 225,000 = 150,000
Solving for x, we get:
x = 4
Therefore, C joined after 4 months.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Let's first calculate the total profit earned by the business: 
Total Profit = Rs.375,000

Let's now calculate the share of A and B in the profit:
Let's assume C joined after x months of A starting the business. 
So, A invested for 12 months, B invested for (12-2) = 10 months, and C invested for (12-x) months.

A's investment = Rs.40,000
B's investment = Rs.60,000
C's investment = Rs.120,000

Total investment = Rs.(40,000*12) + Rs.(60,000*10) + Rs.(120,000*(12-x))
Total investment = Rs.480,000 + Rs.600,000 + Rs.(1,440,000 - 120,000x)
Total investment = Rs.2,520,000 - Rs.120,000x

A's share in the profit = (A's investment / Total investment) * Total Profit
A's share = (40,000 / 2,520,000) * 375,000
A's share = Rs.6,000

B's share in the profit = (B's investment / Total investment) * Total Profit
B's share = (60,000 / 2,520,000) * 375,000
B's share = Rs.9,375

Now, we can calculate C's share in the profit:
C's share = Total Profit - (A's share + B's share)
C's share = 375,000 - (6,000 + 9,375)
C's share = Rs.359,625

We know that C's share in the profit is Rs.150,000. So, we can equate the two and solve for x:
C's share = Rs.359,625
C's investment = Rs.120,000
(C's investment / Total investment) * Total Profit = C's share
(120,000 / (2,520,000 - 120,000x)) * 375,000 = 150,000
Solving for x, we get x = 4

Therefore, C joined the business after 4 months of B joining the business.

Question: The monthly salary S of a shop assistant is the sum of a fixed salary of $500 plus 5% of all monthly sales. What should the monthly sales be so that her monthly salary reaches $1500?
Choices:
  A: $50000
  B: $40000
  C: $30000
  D: $20000
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The monthly salary S of a shop assistant is the sum of a fixed salary of $500 plus 5% of all monthly sales.
  We need to find the monthly sales that will result in a monthly salary of $1500.
  
Solution:
  Let's assume the monthly sales to be x.
  The monthly salary S is given by S = 500 + 0.05x.
  We need to find the value of x for which S = 1500.
  1500 = 500 + 0.05x
  1000 = 0.05x
  x = 1000/0.05
  x = 20000
  
Therefore, the monthly sales should be $20000 for the shop assistant to reach a monthly salary of $1500.
Action: Answer("D")

  D: If monthly sales were $20000, then the monthly salary would be (0.05 * 20000) + 500 = $1500, which is equal to $1500.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 57 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The sum of k consecutive integers is 51. If the least integer is -50, then k =
Choices:
  A: 40
  B: 62
  C: 82
  D: 92
  E: 102
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If we have k consecutive integers, then the sum of these integers is equal to k times the average of these integers.
  The average of k consecutive integers starting from n is (n + (n + k - 1))/2 = (2n + k - 1)/2.
  We can use this formula to solve the problem.
  
Solution:
  Let's call the least integer "n". We know that n = -50.
  We also know that the sum of k consecutive integers is 51.
  So we can write an equation: k * (2n + k - 1)/2 = 51
  Plugging in n = -50, we get: k * (-99 + k)/2 = 51
  Multiplying both sides by 2, we get: k * (-99 + k) = 102
  Rearranging, we get: k^2 - 99k + 102 = 0
  Using the quadratic formula, we get: k = (99  sqrt(99^2 - 4*102))/2
  k = (99  sqrt(9705))/2
  Since k has to be a positive integer, we take the positive root: k = (99 + sqrt(9705))/2
  k  40.96
  Since k has to be an integer, the closest integer to 40.96 is 41.
  
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  If we have k consecutive integers starting from n, then the sum of these integers is given by k * n + k(k-1)/2.
  We are given that the least integer is -50.
  We are also given that the sum of k consecutive integers is 51.
  
Solution:
  Let's assume that the k consecutive integers start from n.
  Then, we can write the sum of k consecutive integers as k * n + k(k-1)/2.
  We are given that the sum of k consecutive integers is 51.
  Therefore, we can write the equation as k * n + k(k-1)/2 = 51.
  We are also given that the least integer is -50.
  Therefore, we can write n = -50.
  Substituting n = -50 in the equation, we get k(-50) + k(k-1)/2 = 51.
  Simplifying the equation, we get k^2 - 49k + 102 = 0.
  Using the quadratic formula, we get k = (49  sqrt(49^2 - 4*1*102))/2.
  Therefore, k = (49  sqrt(2401 - 408))/2 = (49  sqrt(1993))/2.
  Since k has to be a positive integer, we can discard the negative root.
  Therefore, k = (49 + sqrt(1993))/2.
  This value is approximately equal to 40.95.
  Since k has to be a positive integer, the closest value to 40.95 is 41.

  E: 3y/(wx)

  There are 60 seconds in a minute.

  The time it will take y gallons to pass through the drain is y/(12w/5) minutes.

Question: A square piece of cloth is trimmed by 4 feet on one edge to form a rectangular piece, which is then cut diagonally in half to create two triangles. If the area of each of triangle is 70 square feet, what was the perimeter (in feet) of the original piece of square cloth?
Choices:
  A: 56
  B: 58
  C: 60
  D: 62
  E: 64
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The original square piece of cloth has four equal sides.
  When trimmed by 4 feet on one edge, the new rectangular piece has two sides that are equal to the length of the original square piece and two sides that are 4 feet shorter.
  The two triangles created by cutting the rectangular piece diagonally in half are congruent.
  The area of a triangle can be calculated as (base x height) / 2.
  The perimeter of a square can be calculated as 4 x side length.
Action: 
  Let x be the length of the original square piece of cloth.
  The rectangular piece has dimensions of x by x-4.
  The area of each triangle is 70, so we have:
  (x(x-4)/2) = 70
  Solving for x, we get x = 10.
  Therefore, the original square piece of cloth had a perimeter of 4x = 40 feet.
  Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The area of a triangle can be calculated as (1/2) * base * height.
  The area of a square can be calculated as side * side.
  The Pythagorean theorem can be used to find the length of the diagonal of a rectangle.
  
Let x be the length of each side of the original square piece of cloth.
After trimming 4 feet from one edge, the length of the rectangular piece is x by (x-4).
Using the Pythagorean theorem, the diagonal of the rectangular piece is sqrt(x^2 + (x-4)^2).
Each of the two triangles has an area of 70 square feet, so the area of the rectangular piece is 140 square feet.
Thus, (x * (x-4)) / 2 = 140, which simplifies to x^2 - 4x - 280 = 0.
Solving for x using the quadratic formula, we get x = 18 or x = -16 (we discard the negative solution).
The perimeter of the original square piece of cloth is 4x.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  - The area of a triangle is given by the formula: (base * height) / 2.

  - The perimeter of a square is given by the formula: 4 * side.

  The area of each triangle is (x-4)*h/2 = 70, where h is the height of the triangle.
  Solving for h, we get h = 140/(x-4).
  The diagonal of the rectangular piece is the hypotenuse of the right triangles, and its length is sqrt((x-4)^2 + x^2).
  By the Pythagorean theorem, we have (x-4)^2 + x^2 = (sqrt(2)*h)^2 = 2h^2.
  Substituting h = 140/(x-4), we get (x-4)^2 + x^2 = 2*(140/(x-4))^2.
  Simplifying and solving for x, we get x = 18.
  Therefore, the perimeter of the original square piece of cloth is 4x = 72.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 61 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A rectangular parking space is marked out by painting three of its sides. If the length of the unpainted side is 9 feet, and the sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet, then what is the area of the parking space in square feet?
Choices:
  A: 46
  B: 81
  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: None
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The painted sides are two adjacent sides and one end of the rectangle.
  Let's call the length of the rectangle l and the width w.
  We know that w = 9 feet.
  The sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet, so we can write an equation: l + 2w = 37.
  We can solve for l: l = 37 - 2w = 37 - 2(9) = 19 feet.
  The area of a rectangle is A = lw.
  Therefore, the area of the parking space is A = l * w = 19 * 9 = 171 square feet.
Action: Answer("E") None of the above. The correct answer is 171 square feet.
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The painted sides of the parking space form a rectangle.
  The length of the unpainted side is opposite to the shorter side of the rectangle.
  Let L be the length of the rectangle and W be the width of the rectangle.
  We know that W = 9 feet and 2L + W = 37 feet.
  Solving for L, we get L = 14 feet.
  The area of the rectangle is A = L * W = 14 * 9 = 126 square feet.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  The parking space is rectangular.
  Three sides of the parking space are painted.
  The length of the unpainted side is 9 feet.
  The sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet.
  We need to find the area of the parking space.
  
Let's assume that the length of the parking space is l and the width of the parking space is w. Then we can write two equations based on the given information:
  2l + w = 37 (sum of the lengths of the painted sides)
  lw = A (area of the parking space)

We can solve for w in the first equation:
  w = 37 - 2l

  l(37 - 2l) = A
  37l - 2l^2 = A

  l + w + 9 = 37
  l + w = 28
  l + (37 - 2l) = 28
  37 - l = 28
  l = 9

  333 - 162 = A
  A = 171

Topic: Math
Question: Hoses A and B spout water at different constant rates, and hose A can fill a certain pool in 8 hours. Hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours and the two hoses, working together, then finished filling the pool in another 3 hours. How many hours would it have taken hose B, working alone, to fill the entire pool?
Choices:
  A: 8
  B: 15
  C: 12
  D: 6
  E: 3
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that hose A can fill the pool in x hours, then its rate of filling is 1/x.
  Let's assume that hose B can fill the pool in y hours, then its rate of filling is 1/y.
  If hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours, then it filled 2/x of the pool.
  If the two hoses, working together, then finished filling the pool in another 3 hours, then their combined rate of filling is 1/3, and the remaining part of the pool (1-2/x) was filled by both hoses in 3 hours.
  Therefore, we can write the equation: 2/x + 3(1/x + 1/y) = 1
  We need to solve for y to find how many hours it would have taken hose B, working alone, to fill the entire pool.
Action: Answer("C")  
Solving the equation: 
  2/x + 3(1/x + 1/y) = 1
  2/x + 3(x+y)/xy = 1
  2xy + 3(x+y) = xy
  3y = xy - 2xy - 3x
  3y = -x(y-3) - 3x
  3y = (3-x)(y+3)
  y = 3(x-3)/(y+3)
  Substituting x=8, we get y=12.
  Therefore, hose B, working alone, would take 12 hours to fill the entire pool. Answer("C")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 64 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Two numbers are in the ratio 3:5. If 9 is subtracted from each, the new numbers are in the ratio 12:23. The smaller number is?
Choices:
  A: 21
  B: 33
  C: 35
  D: 42
  E: 58
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let the two numbers be 3x and 5x.
  If 9 is subtracted from each, the new numbers are 3x-9 and 5x-9.
  We are given that (3x-9)/(5x-9) = 12/23.
  We can solve for x using this equation and then find the value of 3x, which is the smaller number.

Calculation:
  (3x-9)/(5x-9) = 12/23
  23(3x-9) = 12(5x-9)
  69x - 207 = 60x - 108
  9x = 99
  x = 11
  Therefore, the smaller number is 3x = 33.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  If two numbers are in the ratio a:b, then they can be written as ax and bx, where x is a common factor and a and b are relatively prime.
  If two numbers are in the ratio a:b, and each is increased or decreased by the same amount, then the new numbers are in the ratio a+k:b+k, where k is the amount added or subtracted.
  
Let the original numbers be 3x and 5x.
After subtracting 9 from each, the new numbers are 3x-9 and 5x-9.
The new ratio is (3x-9):(5x-9) = 12:23.

To solve for x, we can cross-multiply:
12(5x-9) = 23(3x-9)
60x - 108 = 69x - 207
9x = 99
x = 11

Therefore, the original numbers are 33 and 55.
The smaller number after subtracting 9 is 33-9 = 24.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  If two numbers are in the ratio a:b, then they can be written as ax and bx, where x is a constant.
  If 9 is subtracted from each number, then the new numbers can be written as (3x - 9) and (5x - 9).
  If (3x - 9) and (5x - 9) are in the ratio 12:23, then (3x - 9) = 12y and (5x - 9) = 23y, where y is a constant.
Action: 
  (3x - 9) = 12y => x = (12y + 9)/3 = 4y + 3
  (5x - 9) = 23y => x = (23y + 9)/5 = 4.6y + 1.8
  Since x is the same in both equations, we can equate them and solve for y:
  4y + 3 = 4.6y + 1.8
  0.6y = 1.2
  y = 2
  Therefore, the smaller number is 3x - 9 = 12y = 24.
  Answer: Answer("A")

Knowledge:

  Solving for x, we get x = 9.
  Therefore, the smaller number is 3x - 9 = 18.

  If 9 is subtracted from each number, then the difference between the numbers remains the same.
  If two numbers are in the ratio a:b, and 9 is subtracted from each, then the new ratio is (a-9):(b-9).

Action: Answer("B")
Response 5:
Knowledge:
  If two numbers are in the ratio a:b, then they can be written as ax and bx, where x is a common factor and a and b are integers.
  If 9 is subtracted from each number, then the difference between the numbers remains the same.
  If two numbers are in the ratio a:b, and 9 is subtracted from each, then the new ratio is (a-9):(b-9).
  
Let the two numbers be 3x and 5x.
After subtracting 9 from each, the new ratio is (3x-9):(5x-9) = 12:23.
We can write this as (3x-9)/(5x-9) = 12/23.
Solving for x, we get x = 69.
Therefore, the smaller number is 3x - 9 = 3(69) - 9 = 198.

Topic: Math
Question: If one of the roots of the quadratic equation x^2 + mx + 22 = 0 is 1.5, then what is the value of m?
Choices:
  A: -23.5
  B: -17.5
  C: -10.5
  D: -16.2
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Quadratic equation is of the form ax^2 + bx + c = 0.
  The sum of the roots of a quadratic equation is -b/a.
  The product of the roots of a quadratic equation is c/a.
  If one of the roots of a quadratic equation is known, then the other root can be found by dividing c/a by the known root and subtracting it from the negative sum of the roots.
  
Let's use the above knowledge to solve the problem:
  Given that one of the roots is 1.5, let's find the other root:
  Sum of the roots = -m/1 = -m
  Product of the roots = 22/1 = 22
  Let the other root be r.
  r = (22/1) / 1.5 = 14.67
  Sum of the roots = 1.5 + 14.67 = 16.17 = -m
  m = -16.17
  
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  A quadratic equation in the form of ax^2 + bx + c = 0 has two roots given by the formula (-b  sqrt(b^2 - 4ac)) / 2a.
  If one of the roots of a quadratic equation is given, then we can use that information to find the other root and ultimately find the value of m.
  If one of the roots is 1.5, then the other root is also 1.5 (since the product of the roots is equal to c/a, which is 22/1 in this case).
  We can use the formula for the sum of the roots (-b/a) to find the value of m.
Action: Answer("A")  
Explanation: 
  Since one of the roots is 1.5, the other root is also 1.5. Therefore, the quadratic equation can be written as x^2 - 3x + 22 = 0.
  Using the formula for the sum of the roots (-b/a), we get -(-3)/1 = 3. Therefore, m = -22 + 3 = -19.
  Checking the answer, we can see that (-19) is equal to (-23.5) + 4.5, which is the value of m obtained by using the quadratic formula with the roots 1.5 and 15.

Knowledge:
  For a quadratic equation of the form ax^2 + bx + c = 0, the sum of the roots is -b/a and the product of the roots is c/a.
  If one root of a quadratic equation is given, then the other root can be found using the product of the roots.
  
Solution:
  The given quadratic equation is x^2 + mx + 22 = 0.
  Let's assume that the other root is r.
  We know that the product of the roots is 22, so we have:
  1.5 * r = 22
  r = 22/1.5
  r = 14.67
  
  The sum of the roots is -m/1, so we have:
  1.5 + 14.67 = -m/1
  16.17 = -m
  m = -16.17
  
  Therefore, the value of m is approximately -16.2.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 66 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In a large forest, 300 deer were caught, tagged, and returned during 2001. During 2002, 500 deer were caught at random, of which only 20 had tags from the previous year. If the percent of deer in the forest that had tags during the second year and were caught in the 500 deer sample is representative of the percent of the total deer population in the forest with tags, what is the total deer population in the forest (assuming no change in population between 2001 and 2002)?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 500
  C: 5000
  D: 6000
  E: 7500
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - We know that 300 deer were tagged in 2001.
  - We know that 20 of the 500 deer caught in 2002 had tags from the previous year.
  - We know that the percentage of deer in the 500 deer sample that had tags is representative of the percentage of the total deer population with tags.
  - We can use proportions to solve the problem.
  
Solution:
  Let x be the total deer population in the forest.
  The percentage of deer with tags in the 500 deer sample is 20/500 = 4%.
  We can set up the proportion: 
  (number of deer with tags in the forest) / x = 4%
  We know that 300 deer were tagged in 2001, so the number of deer with tags in the forest is 300 + (number of deer with tags in 2002).
  In 2002, 20 deer were caught with tags, so the number of deer with tags in 2002 is 20 / (500/ x).
  Putting it all together:
  (300 + 20 / (500/x)) / x = 0.04
  Solving for x:
  300 + 20 / (500/x) = 0.04x
  300x + 20(500) = 20x
  300x = 10000
  x = 10000 / 300 = 33.33...  33,333
  
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  - In 2001, 300 deer were tagged and released into the forest.
  - In 2002, 500 deer were caught, and 20 of them had tags from the previous year.
  - We are assuming that the percentage of tagged deer in the sample is representative of the percentage of tagged deer in the entire population.
  - Let's call the total deer population "x".

Let's set up an equation to solve for "x":
- The number of tagged deer in the sample is 20, which represents some percentage of the total population: 20 = (x / 100) * p, where "p" is the percentage of the total population that is sampled.
- We know that the sample size is 500, so p = (500 / x) * 100.
- Substituting this into the first equation, we get: 20 = (x / 100) * ((500 / x) * 100)
- Simplifying this equation, we get: 20 = 500 / x * 100
- Dividing both sides by 100, we get: 0.2 = 5 / x
- Multiplying both sides by "x", we get: x * 0.2 = 5
- Dividing both sides by 0.2, we get: x = 25

Action: Answer("E") 
The total deer population in the forest is 7500.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 68 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: On dividing 2272 and 875 by a 3-digit number N, we get the same remainder. The sum of the digits of N is:
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 11
  C: 12
  D: 13
  E: 14
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If two numbers have the same remainder when divided by a third number, then their difference is divisible by that third number.
  If a number is divisible by a certain integer, then the sum of its digits is also divisible by that integer.
  
Solution:
Let the common remainder be x. Then, we have:
  2272 = aN + x
  875 = bN + x
where a and b are integers.

Question: By himself, Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours. On a particular day, he happens to finish two-thirds of the work. The remaining portion of the work is done by Jill, whose rate of cleaning is just 5% of what Jack can do. How long does it take Jill to finish the remaining work?
Choices:
  A: 4
  B: 8
  C: 22
  D: 50
  E: 20
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours, then he can clean 1/12 of the yacht in one hour.
  If Jack finished two-thirds of the work, then there is one-third of the work remaining.
  If Jill's rate of cleaning is just 5% of what Jack can do, then she can clean 1/20 of what Jack can do in one hour.
  Let's call the time it takes Jill to finish the remaining work "t".
  We can use the formula: Work = Rate x Time

Calculation:
  Jack finished two-thirds of the work, so there is one-third of the work remaining.
  Let's call the total work "W".
  Then, the remaining work is (1/3)W.
  Jack can clean 1/12 of the yacht in one hour, so his rate is 1/12.
  Jill's rate is 1/20 of Jack's rate, so her rate is (1/20)(1/12) = 1/240.
  We can set up the equation: (1/3)W = (1/12)t + (1/240)t
  Simplifying the right side: (1/12 + 1/240)t = (1/3)W
  Combining the fractions: (1/10)t = (1/3)W
  Solving for "t": t = (3/10)W

Action: Answer("E")  
The time it takes Jill to finish the remaining work is (3/10) times the total work. We don't know the total work, but we can see that the only answer choice that is a multiple of (3/10) is E: 20. Therefore, the answer is E.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 70 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Mr.Sam takes 17 hours to go by train to a certain city and return by car. He loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train. How long would he have taken if he had traveled by car in both ways?
Choices:
  A: 22 hrs
  B: 18 hrs
  C: 16 hrs
  D: 20 hrs
  E: 13 hrs
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume the time taken by Mr. Sam to travel to the city by train is T1 and the time taken to return by car is T2.
  We know that T1 + T2 = 17 and T1-4 = T2
  We need to find T2+T2 = 2T2
  
Calculation:
  From T1 + T2 = 17, we can get T1 = 17 - T2
  Substituting T1 in T1-4 = T2, we get (17 - T2) - 4 = T2
  Solving the above equation, we get T2 = 11
  Therefore, T2 + T2 = 2T2 = 22
  
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Let's assume that the time Mr. Sam takes to travel one way by train is "t" hours. 

Knowledge:
  - Mr. Sam takes 17 hours to go by train to a certain city and return by car.
  - He loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train.

If he goes by train to the city and returns by car, the total time he would take is:
t + 17 + t - 4 = 2t + 13 hours

If he goes both ways by car, the total time he would take is:
2t - 4 hours

We know that the two times are equal, so:

2t + 13 = 2t - 4

Solving for "t", we get:

t = 17/2

Substituting this value in the equation for the time taken if he goes both ways by car, we get:

2t - 4 = 2(17/2) - 4 = 13

Therefore, Mr. Sam would take 13 hours if he had traveled by car in both ways.

Response 4:
Let's assume that the time Mr. Sam takes to go to the city by train is "x" hours. Therefore, the time he takes to return by car is (17 - x) hours. 

According to the problem, if he goes both ways by train, he loses 4 hours. This means that the total time he would take if he goes both ways by train is (2x + 4) hours. 

We know that the total time he takes to go by train and return by car is 17 hours. Therefore, we can set up the following equation: 

x + (17 - x) = 17 - (2x + 4)

Simplifying this equation, we get: 

x - 2x = 17 - 17 + 4

-x = 4

x = -4 (which is not a valid solution)

This means that our assumption that Mr. Sam takes "x" hours to go to the city by train is incorrect. Therefore, we need to try a different approach. 

Let's assume that the time Mr. Sam takes to go to the city by car is "y" hours. Therefore, the time he takes to return by car is also "y" hours. 

According to the problem, if he goes both ways by train, he loses 4 hours. This means that the total time he would take if he goes both ways by train is (2x + 4) hours. 

We know that the total time he takes to go by train and return by car is 17 hours. Therefore, we can set up the following equation: 

y + y + 4 = 17

Simplifying this equation, we get: 

2y = 13

y = 6.5

Therefore, Mr. Sam would take 6.5 hours if he had traveled by car in both ways.

Topic: Math
Question: For bringing each copper coin from the bottom of a river, a coin-diver gets 20 cents, and for each brass coin she gets 25 cents. If after one dive, she got $3.40. What is the minimum number of copper coins that she brought?
Choices:
  A: 4
  B: 3
  C: 2
  D: 1
  E: 0
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the number of copper coins is "x" and the number of brass coins is "y".
  The amount of money she gets for each copper coin is 20 cents.
  The amount of money she gets for each brass coin is 25 cents.
  The total amount of money she got after one dive is $3.40.
  We can write two equations based on the information given in the question:
  1. 20x + 25y = 340 (in cents)
  2. x + y = total number of coins
  
To solve this problem, we need to find the minimum number of copper coins. 

Solution:
  We can use the second equation to find the value of y in terms of x:
  y = total number of coins - x
  
  We can substitute this value of y in the first equation:
  20x + 25(total number of coins - x) = 340
  
  Simplifying this equation, we get:
  5x + 25(total number of coins) = 340
  
  We know that x has to be an integer value, so we can try different values of x to see which one satisfies the equation. 
  If we start with x = 1, then y = total number of coins - 1.
  Substituting these values in the equation, we get:
  5(1) + 25(total number of coins) = 340
  25(total number of coins) = 335
  total number of coins = 13.4
  
  Since the total number of coins has to be an integer value, we can try the next value of x, which is x = 2.
  y = total number of coins - 2
  Substituting these values in the equation, we get:
  5(2) + 25(total number of coins - 2) = 340
  25(total number of coins) = 350
  total number of coins = 14
  
  So, the minimum number of copper coins that she brought is 2.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 72 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The sum of the digits of a three digit number is 17, and the sum of the squares of its digits is 109. If we subtract 495 from the number, we shall get a number consisting of the same digits written in the reverse order. Find the number.
Choices:
  A: 368
  B: 377
  C: 288
  D: 997
  E: 112
Response 0:
Let's call the hundreds digit of the number "a", the tens digit "b", and the units digit "c". Then we know that:
- a + b + c = 17
- a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 109

We also know that if we subtract 495 from the number, we get a number with the same digits in reverse order. This means that:
- 100a + 10b + c - 495 = 100c + 10b + a

Simplifying this equation, we get:
- 99a - 99c = 495
- a - c = 5

We can use the first equation (a + b + c = 17) and the third equation (a - c = 5) to solve for a and c in terms of b:
- a = 6 + b
- c = b - 1

Substituting these expressions for a and c into the equation a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 109 and simplifying, we get:
- 3b^2 - 6b - 4 = 0
- b^2 - 2b - 4/3 = 0
- b = 1/2  (13/3)/2

Since b must be an integer, we can only take the positive root:
- b = 1/2 + (13/3)/2  2.56

This means that a  8.56 and c  1.56. Since a and c must be integers, we round them to 9 and 2, respectively. Therefore, the original number is 929, and we can check that 929 - 495 = 434, which has the same digits in reverse order.

A - C = 5

2A + B = 22
Since A is a digit, it must be less than or equal to 9. We can try different values of A to see which one works:
If A = 1, then B = 20/2 = 10, which is not a digit.
If A = 2, then B = 18/2 = 9, which is a digit.
Therefore, A = 2, and B = 9. We can substitute these values into equation (2) to solve for C:

C^2 = 109 - 85
C^2 = 24
C = 4 (since C is a digit)
Therefore, the three digit number is 299, and the number with the same digits in reverse order is 992. We can verify that 992 - 495 = 497, which has the same digits as 299 in reverse order.

A^2 + B^2 + C^2 = 109  (equation 2)

100A - A + 10B - 10B + C - 100C = 495
99A - 99C = 495
A - C = 5  (equation 4)

2C + B = 12  (equation 5)

B^2 = 109 - (A - C)(A + C)
B^2 = 109 - 5(17)
B^2 = 24
B = 2 or -2

Since B is a digit, we must have B = 2. Substituting this into equation 5, we get:
2C + 2 = 12
C = 5

Finally, we can use A = C + 5 and B = 2 to find the original number:
ABC = 525
Subtracting 495 from this, we get 030, which is the same as 30. Therefore, the original number is 525, and the answer is (D) 997.

Question: The ratio of the volumes of a cube to that of the sphere which will fit inside the cube is?
Choices:
  A: 2: 
  B: 7:2
  C: 8:2
  D: 6: 
  E: 8:3
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The volume of a cube is given by V_cube = s^3, where s is the length of one side of the cube.
  The volume of a sphere is given by V_sphere = (4/3)r^3, where r is the radius of the sphere.
  If a sphere is inscribed inside a cube, then the diameter of the sphere is equal to the edge length of the cube.

To solve this problem, we need to find the ratio of the volumes of the cube to the sphere. We can do this by comparing their formulas.

V_cube / V_sphere = (s^3) / [(4/3)(r^3)]

Since the diameter of the sphere is equal to the edge length of the cube, we have:

r = s/2

Substituting this into the above equation, we get:

V_cube / V_sphere = (s^3) / [(4/3)((s/2)^3)]
                  = (s^3) / [(4/3)(s^3/8)]
                  = 2/3

Action: Answer("A")

  The diameter of the sphere that fits inside the cube is equal to the length of the side of the cube.
  The ratio of the volumes of the cube to the sphere is V_cube/V_sphere.
  The radius of the sphere is equal to half of the length of the side of the cube.
  Therefore, V_sphere = (4/3)(a/2)^3 = (1/6)a^3.
  So, V_cube/V_sphere = a^3/[(1/6)a^3] = 6/.

  This problem involves counting the number of ways to divide 10 lime soda bottles into two groups of 5 each.
  The formula for the number of ways to choose k items from a set of n distinct items is given by the binomial coefficient C(n,k) = n! / (k! * (n-k)!).
  The formula for the number of ways to divide n distinct items into k distinct groups is given by the Stirling number of the second kind S(n,k).
  The Stirling number of the second kind S(n,k) represents the number of ways to partition a set of n distinct items into k non-empty subsets.
  The Stirling number of the second kind S(n,k) is defined recursively by S(n,k) = k*S(n-1,k) + S(n-1,k-1).
  In this problem, we want to partition a set of 10 distinct items into 2 non-empty subsets, so the answer is S(10,2).

The first group of 5 can be chosen in 10C5 ways, which is equal to 252. After the first group is chosen, the second group is automatically determined. Therefore, there is only one way to choose the second group. 

Answer: Answer("252")

Question: All 250 files on Sam's hard drive are infected by either a virus or a worm or both. The number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm. If 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, how many of Sam's files were NOT infected by a worm?
Choices:
  A: 50
  B: 70
  C: 75
  D: 100
  E: 125
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - Let V be the number of files infected by a virus only.
  - Let W be the number of files infected by a worm only.
  - Let B be the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm.
  - We know that V + W + B = 250.
  - We also know that W = 2.5B.
  - We want to find the number of files that were not infected by a worm.
  - We know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, so V + B = 0.5(250) = 125.
  - We can use these equations to solve for W, and then subtract from 250 to find the number of files not infected by a worm.
  
Calculation:
  - Substituting W = 2.5B into the equation V + W + B = 250, we get V + 3.5B = 250.
  - Substituting V + B = 125 into the equation above, we get B = 25 and V = 100.
  - Therefore, W = 2.5B = 62.5.
  - The number of files not infected by a worm is V + B = 125.
  - Therefore, the answer is 125.

Topic: Math
Question: A trader sold an article at a profit of 20% for Rs.360. What is the cost price of the article?
Choices:
  A: 270
  B: 300
  C: 280
  D: 320
  E: 315
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Profit% = (Profit / Cost Price) * 100
  Selling Price = Cost Price + Profit
  We can use these formulas to solve the problem.
  
Let's assume the cost price of the article is "x".
The profit percentage is given as 20%.
Therefore, the profit made by the trader is (20/100)*x = 0.2x
The selling price is given as Rs.360.
Therefore, we can write the equation as:
Selling Price = Cost Price + Profit
360 = x + 0.2x
360 = 1.2x
x = 360/1.2
x = 300

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Profit% = (Profit / Cost Price) x 100
  Selling Price = Cost Price + Profit
  We can use these formulas to solve the problem.

Selling Price = Rs. 360

20 = (360 - x) / x x 100
2000 = 360 - x
x = 360 - 2000
x = 300
Therefore, the cost price of the article is Rs. 300.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 78 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A newspaper costs $4 on Sunday and $1 the rest of the days of the week. If a hotel orders twice as many papers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week and pays $210 per week for newspapers, how many newspapers does it buy on Monday?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 30
  C: 45
  D: 60
  E: 75
Response 0:

  Let's assume that the hotel buys x newspapers on Monday.
  The hotel buys twice as many newspapers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week, which means it buys 2x newspapers on Sunday.
  The hotel pays $4 for each newspaper on Sunday and $1 for each newspaper on the rest of the days of the week.
  The hotel pays $210 per week for newspapers.
  The total number of newspapers the hotel buys per week is 2x + x*5 = 7x.
  The total cost of the newspapers per week is 4*(2x) + 1*(5x) = 13x.
  We know that 13x = 210, which means x = 16.15 (rounded to two decimal places).

Topic: Math
Question: Allen starts from X, goes to Y. At the same time Bob starts from Y and goes towards X. Once Allen reaches Y he changes his direction and returns to X. Once Bob reaches X, he changes his direction and returns to Y. Throughout Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Find the distance between X and Y.
Choices:
  A: 144km
  B: 72 km
  C: 126km
  D: 84 km
  E: 48km
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - Allen and Bob start at opposite points and move towards each other.
  - Allen and Bob switch directions once they reach their destination.
  - Allen's speed is 54 kmph and Bob's speed is 78 kmph.
  - Bob covers 48 km more than Allen by the time they meet for the second time.
  - We need to find the distance between X and Y.
  
Let's assume that the distance between X and Y is d km.

When Allen and Bob meet for the first time, they have covered a total distance of d km. Let's assume that they meet after t hours. 

In t hours, Allen covers a distance of 54t km and Bob covers a distance of 78t km. Since they meet at the midpoint, we can say that:

54t + 78t = d

132t = d

t = d/132

When they meet for the second time, Allen would have covered a distance of 2d km (since he travels from Y to X and then back to Y). Bob would have covered a distance of 2d + 48 km (since he covers 48 km more than Allen). 

We know that they meet at the midpoint, so:

2d + 48 = d

d = 48 km

Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Let the distance between X and Y be d. 

When Allen and Bob meet for the first time, they have together covered a distance of d. 

Let's say Allen travels a distance of x to reach Y. Therefore, Bob travels a distance of (d - x) to reach Y at the same time. 

Time taken by Allen to travel x km = x/54
Time taken by Bob to travel (d - x) km = (d - x)/78

Since they meet at the same time, we can equate the time taken by both of them:
x/54 = (d - x)/78

Solving the above equation, we get:
x = 3d/7

Therefore, the distance covered by Bob to meet Allen for the first time is:
d - x = 4d/7

When they meet for the second time, Allen would have covered a distance of 2x, and Bob would have covered a distance of 2(d - x). 

We are given that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Therefore:
2(d - x) - 2x = 2d/7 + 48

Solving the above equation, we get:
d = 252 km

Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 252 km.

Question: The number of water lilies on a certain lake doubles every two days. If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. In how many days will the lake be fully covered with lilies, if initially there were 64 water lilies on it?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 28
  C: 30
  D: 53
  E: 59
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  If the number of water lilies doubles every two days, then the number of water lilies after n days is 2^(n/2) times the initial number of water lilies.
  If it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies starting from one water lily, then the number of water lilies after 60 days is 2^(60/2) = 2^30.
Action: 
  The initial number of water lilies is 64, which is 2^6.
  Let's find out how many days it takes for the number of water lilies to reach 2^30 from 2^6:
  2^6 * 2^(n/2) = 2^30
  2^(n/2) = 2^(30-6)
  n/2 = 24
  n = 48
  Therefore, it takes 48 days for the lake to be fully covered with lilies if initially there were 64 water lilies on it.
  Answer: Answer("D")

Knowledge:
  If the number of water lilies doubles every two days, then the growth rate is exponential.
  If the lake is fully covered with water lilies after 60 days with one water lily initially, then the growth rate is such that 2^30 = 2^60/2 = the number of water lilies after 60 days with one water lily initially.
  If initially there were 64 water lilies on the lake, then the growth rate is such that 2^x = 2^6 * 2^x-6 = the number of water lilies after x days with 64 water lilies initially.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 83 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another?
Choices:
  A: 1 hr 23 min
  B: 1 hr 15 min
  C: 1 hr 8 min
  D: 56 min
  E: 55 min
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9 am, so it takes 4 hours to travel from A to B.
  Train N leaves City B at 7 am and reaches City A at 10:30 am, so it takes 3.5 hours to travel from B to A.
  The two trains are traveling towards each other.
Action: 
  Let's find the time difference between when Train N starts and when Train M starts: 7 am - 5 am = 2 hours.
  During this time, Train N travels for 2 hours and Train M travels for 0 hours.
  Let's call the distance between City A and City B "D". Since the two trains are traveling towards each other, their relative speed is the sum of their speeds.
  Let's call the speed of Train M "vM" and the speed of Train N "vN".
  Then, the relative speed of the two trains is vM + vN.
  We know that Train M travels the entire distance D, and Train N travels the entire distance D as well.
  Let's call the time it takes for the two trains to meet "t".
  Then, we can write the equation: D = vM * t + vN * t.
  Solving for t, we get t = D / (vM + vN).
  Plugging in the values we know, we get t = D / (4 + 3.5) = D / 7.5.
  We also know that Train N starts at 7 am and travels for t hours to meet Train M.
  Therefore, the time they meet is 7 am + t hours.
  Plugging in t = D / 7.5, we get 7 am + D / 7.5 hours.
  We just need to find the value of D to get the final answer.
  We know that Train M travels for 4 hours at a constant speed, so we can use the formula distance = speed * time to find D.
  D = vM * tM = vN * tN, where tM = 4 hours and tN = 3.5 hours.
  Therefore, D = vM * 4 = vN * 3.5.
  We don't know the speeds of the trains, but we can use the fact that Train N travels 1.5 hours less than Train M to set up an equation.
  Let's call the speed of Train M "x" and the speed of Train N "y".
  Then, we have the equations: 4x = 3.5y + D and D = 1.5y.
  Substituting the second equation into the first equation, we get: 4x = 3.5y + 1.5y = 5y.
  Therefore, y = 4x / 5.
  Substituting this into D = 1.5y, we get D = 6x / 5.
  Plugging in this value of D into the equation we found earlier, we get t = (6x / 5) / 7.5 = 8x / 75.
  Therefore, the time the two trains meet is 7 am + (8x / 75) hours.
  We don't know the value of x, but we can simplify the expression by dividing both the numerator and denominator by 8.
  The final answer is 7 am + (x / 9.375) hours, which is approximately 7:51 am.
  Answer: Answer("C")

  Train M travels for 4 hours, so the distance it covers is d = 4s (where s is the speed of the train).
  Train N travels for 3.5 hours, so the distance it covers is d = 3.5r (where r is the speed of the train).

  Therefore, 4s + 3.5r = D, where D is the distance between City A and City B.

  4s / 3.5r = D / D
  Simplifying, we get:
  s / r = 7 / 8
  Now we can use this ratio to find the time when the two trains meet.
  Let t be the time when Train N and Train M meet.
  Then, Train M travels for t hours and Train N travels for (t - 2) hours (since Train N leaves 2 hours after Train M).
  Using the formula time = distance / speed, we can write:
  t = 4s / (s + r)  (for Train M)
  t - 2 = 3.5r / (s + r)  (for Train N)
  Substituting s / r = 7 / 8, we get:
  t = 16 / 15 hours
  Therefore, the two trains cross each other 16/15 hours after Train M leaves City A.
  To find the time, we add this to the starting time of Train M:
  5:00 am + 1 hr 4 min = 6:04 am

Choices:
  A: 40.8
  B: 41.6
  C: 42.2
  D: 43.5
  E: 44.8
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The formula for the arithmetic mean is: sum of all values / number of values.
  Let's call the sum of the weights of the 10 vehicles "S" and the weight of the new heavy duty truck "x".
  We know that (S/10) = 12.2 and ((S+x)/11) = 14.8 (because the new average is 2.6 tons more than the original average).
  We can use these two equations to solve for x.

Calculation:
  Multiplying the first equation by 10 gives us S = 122.
  Multiplying the second equation by 11 gives us S + x = 162.8.
  Subtracting the first equation from the second equation gives us x = 40.8.

Question: 10kg of a mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay. In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand how much of the mixture is to be removed and replaced with pure sand?
Choices:
  A: 10/7
  B: 20/7
  C: 30/7
  D: 40/7
  E: 50/7
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The initial mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay.
  We want to remove and replace some of the mixture with pure sand to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand.
  Let's assume that we need to remove and replace x kg of the mixture.
  After removing and replacing x kg of the mixture, the amount of sand in the mixture will be 0.5(10-x) kg.
  The amount of clay in the mixture will also be 0.5(10-x) kg.
  We can set up an equation to solve for x.
  The amount of sand in the new mixture is 0.5(10-x) + x kg.
  This is equal to the amount of clay in the new mixture, which is 0.5(10-x) kg.
  So, we have the equation: 0.5(10-x) + x = 0.5(10-x)
  Solving for x, we get x = 20/7.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The current mixture is 30% sand and 70% clay.
  - We want to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand.
  - We need to remove some of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.
  
Solution:
  - Let's assume that we have 10 kg of mixture.
  - The amount of sand in the mixture is 30% of 10 kg, which is 3 kg.
  - The amount of clay in the mixture is 70% of 10 kg, which is 7 kg.
  - In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand, we need to have 5 kg of each.
  - We need to remove some of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.
  - Let's say we remove x kg of the mixture.
  - The amount of sand in the remaining mixture is still 3 kg, but it is now 50% of the mixture.
  - So, we need to add x kg of pure sand to the mixture.
  - The amount of sand in the new mixture is (3 + x) kg, and it is now 5 kg (or 50%) of the mixture.
  - We can set up an equation to solve for x:
      - 0.3 * (10 - x) + x = 0.5 * (10)
      - Simplifying the equation, we get:
          - 3 - 0.3x + x = 5
          - 0.7x = 2
          - x = 20/7
  - Therefore, we need to remove 20/7 kg of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.

  For 12 people, Jill will need to buy 12 * 1.25 = 15 bottles of soda.

  We don't know how much soda each person drinks, but we can assume that the amount of soda needed is proportional to the number of people attending.

  We can solve for x by cross-multiplying: 8x = 120, x = 15/2 = 7.5

Question: What will be the cost of gardening 1-metre  broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre?
Choices:
  A: 3400
  B: 1700
  C: 3440
  D: Cannot be determined
  E: None of these

Knowledge: 
  The perimeter of a rectangle is the sum of all its sides.
  Let's assume that the length and width of the rectangular plot are L and W, respectively.
  The perimeter of the rectangular plot is given by 2(L+W) = 340.
  Therefore, L+W = 170.
  The cost of gardening 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot is equal to the cost of gardening (L+2)(W+2) square meters at the rate of 10 per square meter.
  This can be simplified as 10(L+2)(W+2).
Action: Answer("C")  
To find the cost, we need to first find the value of L and W. We have one equation L+W=170 and we need another equation to solve for L and W. We know that the area of the rectangular plot is LW. We also know that the perimeter is 340. Therefore, 2(L+W) = 340 or L+W=170. We can use this equation to solve for one of the variables. Let's solve for L: L = 170 - W. Now we can substitute this value of L in the equation for the area: LW = (170-W)W = 170W - W^2. We want to find the cost of gardening 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot, which is equal to the cost of gardening (L+2)(W+2) square meters at the rate of 10 per square meter. Substituting L = 170 - W, we get the cost as 10(172 - W - W + 2) = 10(174 - 2W) = 1740 - 20W. Therefore, the cost of gardening 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot is 1740 - 20W. To find the value of W, we need to maximize the area LW. The maximum area occurs when L = W = 85. Therefore, the cost of gardening 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot is 1740 - 20(85) = 1740 - 1700 = 40. Answer("C").

Question: The capacity of a tank of dimensions (8 m  6 m  2.5 m) is
Choices:
  A: 120 litres
  B: 1200 litres
  C: 12000 litres
  D: 120000 litres
  E: None of these
Response 0:

  The formula for calculating the volume of a rectangular tank is V = l  w  h, where l is the length, w is the width, and h is the height.
  The dimensions of the tank are given as 8 m  6 m  2.5 m.
Action: 
  The volume of the tank is V = 8 m  6 m  2.5 m = 120 m^3
  1 m^3 is equal to 1000 litres.
  Therefore, the capacity of the tank is 120 m^3  1000 litres/m^3 = 120000 litres.
  Answer("D")

  The dimensions of the tank are given as 8 m  6 m  2.5 m.

  1 cubic meter is equal to 1000 liters.
  Therefore, the capacity of the tank is 120  1000 = 120000 litres.

Topic: Math
Question: Calculate the percentage gain of a merchant who purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450 and sold the whole lot at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg.
Choices:
  A: 50 %
  B: 60 %
  C: 55 %
  D: 70 %
  E: 58%
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Percentage Gain = (Profit / Cost Price) x 100
  Profit = Selling Price - Cost Price
  Cost Price = (Quantity Purchased x Rate per kg)
  Selling Price = (Quantity Purchased x Selling Rate per kg)
  
Calculation:
  Cost Price = (90 kg x Rs. 5 per kg) = Rs. 450
  Selling Price = (90 kg x Rs. 7.50 per kg) = Rs. 675
  Profit = Selling Price - Cost Price = Rs. 225
  Percentage Gain = (Profit / Cost Price) x 100 = (225 / 450) x 100 = 50%

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Percentage gain = [(Profit/Cost Price) x 100]
  Cost Price = Rs. 450
  Selling Price = Rs. (90 x 7.50) = Rs. 675
  Profit = Selling Price - Cost Price = Rs. (675 - 450) = Rs. 225
Action: 
  Percentage gain = [(Profit/Cost Price) x 100] = [(225/450) x 100] = 50%
  Answer: A
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Percentage gain is calculated as (Profit/Cost Price) x 100
  Cost price is the price at which the merchant purchased the oranges.
  Profit is the difference between the selling price and the cost price.
  Selling price is the price at which the merchant sold the oranges.
  
Calculation:
  Cost price of 1 kg of orange = 450/90 = Rs. 5
  Selling price of 1 kg of orange = Rs. 7.50
  Profit on 1 kg of orange = Selling price - Cost price = 7.50 - 5 = Rs. 2.50
  Total Profit = Profit on 1 kg x 90 kg = Rs. 225
  Percentage gain = (Profit/Cost Price) x 100 = (225/450) x 100 = 50%

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joes fathers age sums up to 100. When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Find the age of Joe's father?
Choices:
  A: 45
  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58
Response 0:
Let's start by defining some variables:
- Let's call Joe's age "J"
- Let's call Joe's sister's age "S"
- Let's call Joe's father's age "F"

From the first sentence, we know that:
J + S + F = 100

From the second sentence, we know that:
J + F = 2(S)

From the third sentence, we know that:
F = 2(S - J)

We can use the second equation to solve for S:
S = (J + F)/2

We can substitute this into the third equation to solve for F:
F = 2((J + F)/2 - J)
F = J + F - 2J
F = 2J

We can substitute this into the first equation to solve for J:
J + S + F = 100
J + (J + F)/2 + F = 100
J + J/2 + F/2 + F = 100
J/2 + 5J/2 = 100
3J = 100
J = 33.33 (repeating)

Now that we know J, we can use the second equation to solve for S:
J + F = 2(S)
F = 2S - J
F = 2(33.33) - J
F = 66.67 - 33.33
F = 33.34

So the age of Joe's father is approximately 33.34 years old.

Action: Answer("None of the above")
Response 1:
Let's assume that Joe's age is "J", Joe's sister's age is "S" and Joe's father's age is "F".

From the first statement, we know that:
J + S + F = 100

From the second statement, we know that:
J + (F - J) = F
S + (F - J) = 2S

Simplifying the second statement, we get:
F - J = F/2 - S/2
F/2 - J/2 = S/2

From the third statement, we know that:
F - J = 2(S - F)
F - J = 2S - 2F
3F - J = 2S

Now we have three equations with three variables:
J + S + F = 100
F/2 - J/2 = S/2
3F - J = 2S

Solving these equations, we get:
J = 18
S = 32
F = 50

Therefore, the age of Joe's father is 50.

J + S + F = 100

From the second statement, we know that when J = F, S + (F - S) * 2 = 2S, which simplifies to:

F - S = S

F = 2S

From the third statement, we know that when J = F, F = 2(S - F + J), which simplifies to:

3F - 2J - 2S = 0

J + S + F = 100

3F - 2J - 2S = 0

J = 50 - F/2

S = F/2

50 - F/2 + F/2 + F = 100

F = 50 * 2 = 100

Therefore, Joe's father's age is F = 100.

Let's start by assigning variables to the ages of Joe, his sister, and his father. Let x be Joe's age, y be his sister's age, and z be his father's age.

From the first sentence, we know that:

x + y + z = 100

From the second sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father:

x + z = 2(y)

Simplifying this equation, we get:

x - 2y + z = 0

From the third sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father, his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Let's call the age of Joe's sister when she was as old as her father "a". At that time, Joe's father was z - a years old, and Joe's sister was y - a years old. So we have:

z - a = 2(y - a)

Simplifying this equation, we get:

2a + z = 2y

Now we have three equations with three variables. We can solve for one variable in terms of the other two and substitute into the other equations to get a system of two equations with two variables. Let's solve for z in terms of x and y from the second equation:

z = 2y - x

Substituting this into the first equation, we get:

x + y + 2y - x = 100

Simplifying, we get:

3y = 100

y = 100/3

Substituting y into the second equation, we get:

x + z = 2(y)

x + 2y - x = 2(y)

2y = 2(y)

This equation is true for any value of y, so we can't solve for x or z yet. But we can use the third equation to get another equation in terms of x and y:

2a + z = 2y

Substituting z = 2y - x, we get:

2a + 2y - x = 2y

2a = x

Substituting this into the second equation, we get:

x + z = 2(y)

x + 2y - x = 2(y)

y = z - x

Substituting y = 100/3 and solving for z, we get:

z = x + 100/3

Substituting x = 2a, we get:

z = 2a + 100/3

Now we have expressions for all three ages in terms of a. Substituting these expressions into the first equation, we get:

2a + 100/3 + 100/3 = 100

Multiplying both sides by 3, we get:

6a + 200 = 300

6a = 100

a = 50/3

Substituting a = 50/3 into the expressions for x, y, and z, we get:

x = 2a = 100/3
y = 100/3
z = 2a + 100/3 = 250/3

So the age of Joe's father is 250/3, which is approximately 83.33.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Each time the coin lands on Heads, Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan.
  Each time the coin lands on Tails, Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher.
  After 20 flips, the net amount won or lost by both Christopher and Jonathan is zero.
  
Solution:
  Let's assume that the coin landed on Heads x times and Tails y times.
  Then, Christopher gave a total of 2x dollars to Jonathan.
  Jonathan gave a total of 3y dollars to Christopher.
  Since the net amount won or lost by both is zero, we have:
  2x - 3y = 0
  2x = 3y
  x = (3/2)y
  Since x and y are integers, y must be even.
  Let's try some values of y to see if we get an integer value of x:
  If y = 2, then x = 3, which is an integer.
  If y = 4, then x = 6, which is an integer.
  If y = 6, then x = 9, which is not an integer.
  Therefore, the coin landed on Heads 3 + 6 = 9 times.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Each time the coin lands on heads, Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan.
  Each time the coin lands on tails, Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher.
  After 20 flips, neither Christopher nor Jonathan won or lost any amount.
  Let's assume the coin landed on heads x times.
  Therefore, the coin landed on tails (20 - x) times.

Calculation:
  Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan x times.
  Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher (20 - x) times.
  The total amount given by Christopher to Jonathan is 2x.
  The total amount given by Jonathan to Christopher is 3(20 - x) = 60 - 3x.
  Since no one won or lost any amount, 2x = 60 - 3x.
  Solving for x, we get x = 12.

Action: Answer("E")

Response 9:
Knowledge:
  Each time the coin lands on Heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan.
  Each time the coin lands on Tails, Jonathan will give $3 to Christopher.
  After flipping the coin 20 times, neither Christopher nor Jonathan won or lost any amount.
  The difference between the number of Heads and the number of Tails multiplied by 2 is equal to the total amount won by either Christopher or Jonathan.
  Therefore, the total amount won by either Christopher or Jonathan must be zero.
  The number of Heads plus the number of Tails must be equal to 20.
  We can use algebra to solve for the number of Heads.

Let x be the number of times the coin landed on Heads.
Then, the number of times the coin landed on Tails is 20 - x.
The total amount won by Christopher is 2x - 3(20 - x) = 5x - 60.
The total amount won by Jonathan is 3(20 - x) - 2x = 60 - x.
Since the total amount won by either Christopher or Jonathan is zero, we have:
5x - 60 = 0

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 97 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Let's assume that there are 'n' employees in the organization and each employee contributes 'x' amount of money. 

So, the total amount collected by 'n' employees is given by: 
Total amount = n * x

According to the question, 
n * x = 6,00,000  ----(1)  (since they want to collect Rs. 6 lakh)

If each employee had contributed Rs. 60 extra, then the new contribution per employee would be (x+60). 
So, the new total amount collected by 'n' employees is given by: 
n * (x+60) = 6,24,000

Expanding the above equation, we get: 
n*x + n*60 = 6,24,000

Substituting the value of n*x from equation (1), we get: 
6,00,000 + n*60 = 6,24,000
n*60 = 24,000
n = 400

Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization. 

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Let's assume that there are 'n' employees in the organization. 
So, the amount contributed by each employee is Rs. (600000/n).
If each employee had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the new amount contributed by each employee would be Rs. ((600000 + 24000)/n) = Rs. (624000/n).
We can set up an equation based on the given information and solve for 'n':
(600000/n) + 60 = (624000/n)
Multiplying both sides by 'n', we get:
600000 + 60n = 624000
Subtracting 600000 from both sides, we get:
60n = 24000
Dividing both sides by 60, we get:
n = 400
Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Let's assume that there are 'x' employees in the organization. 

Knowledge:
  If each employee contributes 'c' amount, then the total contribution will be 'x*c'.
  According to the question, 'x*c = 6,00,000'.
  If each employee contributes 'c+60' amount, then the total contribution will be 'x*(c+60)'.
  According to the question, 'x*(c+60) = 6,24,000'.

Now, we can form two equations using the above information and solve for 'x'.

Equation 1: x*c = 6,00,000
Equation 2: x*(c+60) = 6,24,000

We can simplify Equation 2 by expanding the left side of the equation.
x*c + 60*x = 6,24,000

We can substitute Equation 1 in the above equation to get:
6,00,000 + 60*x = 6,24,000
60*x = 24,000
x = 400

Action: Answer("C") 
Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.

Question: A man divides Rs 8600 among 5 sons, 4 daughters and 2 nephews. If each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew, and each son receives five as much as each nephew. How much does each daughter receive ?
Choices:
  A: Rs 400
  B: Rs 500
  C: Rs 600
  D: Rs 700
  E: Rs 800
Response 0:
Let the amount each nephew receives be x.
Then, each daughter receives 4x and each son receives 5x.
Total number of people = 5 + 4 + 2 = 11
Total amount = Rs 8600
Amount received by daughters = 4x * 4 * 4 = 64x
Amount received by sons = 5x * 5 = 25x
Amount received by nephews = 2x * x = 2x^2
Total amount received = 64x * 4 + 25x * 5 + 2x^2 = 8600
256x + 125x + 2x^2 = 8600
2x^2 + 381x - 8600 = 0
Solving this quadratic equation, we get x = 20 or -212.5 (which is not possible)
Therefore, each nephew receives Rs 20.
Each daughter receives 4x = 4 * 20 = Rs 80.
Hence, the answer is A: Rs 400. 
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:

Each son receives 5 times as much as each nephew, so each son receives 5x.

The total amount divided is Rs 8600.
Therefore, we have the equation:
5(5x) + 4(4x) + 2(x) = 8600
Simplifying and solving for x, we get:
35x = 8600
x = 8600/35 = 246.29 (rounded to two decimal places)
Each daughter receives 4x = 4(246.29) = 985.16 (rounded to two decimal places)

Topic: Math
Question: A student instead of finding the value of 7/8 of a number, found the value of 7/18 of the number. If his answer differed from the actual one by 770, find the that number.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 2520
  C: 1728
  D: 1656
  E: None
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume the number is "x".
  The student found the value of 7/18 of the number, which is (7/18)x.
  The student should have found the value of 7/8 of the number, which is (7/8)x.
  The difference between the two values is 770.
  We can set up an equation: (7/8)x - (7/18)x = 770
  We can simplify the equation by finding the least common multiple of 8 and 18, which is 72. 
  Multiplying both sides by 72, we get: 63x - 28x = 55440
  Solving for x, we get: x = 2520.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let the number be x.
  The student found the value of 7/18 of the number, instead of 7/8 of the number.
  The student's answer differed from the actual one by 770.
  We can use the formula: Error = Actual Value - Approximate Value
  
Calculation:
  Let's find the actual value of 7/8 of the number:
  7/8 * x = Actual Value
  
  Let's find the approximate value of 7/18 of the number:
  7/18 * x = Approximate Value
  
  Let's find the error:
  Error = Actual Value - Approximate Value
  Error = 7/8 * x - 7/18 * x
  Error = 77/72 * x
  
  We know that the error is 770, so we can solve for x:
  77/72 * x = 770
  x = 770 * 72 / 77
  x = 720
  
Action: Answer("E") None of the above. 
The calculated value of x is not one of the choices provided.

  We can simplify this equation to get (35/72)*x = 770.
  Solving for x, we get x = (770*72)/35 = 1584.

Topic: Math
Question: Calculate the maximum distance you can travel with $8.50 on a cab which charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
Choices:
  A: 11.75 miles
  B: 12.75 miles
  C: 17.75 miles
  D: 14.75 miles
  E: 10.75 miles
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The cab charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile, which is 0.25 miles.
  The cab charges 10 cents for each additional quarter-mile.
  We need to find the maximum distance we can travel with $8.50.

Calculation:
  We can start by finding how much of the $8.50 is used up by the initial $3.50 charge:
  $8.50 - $3.50 = $5.00
  We can then divide the remaining $5.00 by the cost per quarter-mile:
  $5.00  $0.10 = 50 quarter-miles
  Since the initial charge covers the first quarter-mile, we can add 0.25 miles to the total distance:
  0.25 + (50  0.25) = 0.25 + 12.50 = 12.75 miles

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The cab charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
  We need to find the maximum distance we can travel with $8.50.

  $8.50 - $3.50 = $5.00
  $5.00 / $0.10 = 50 quarters = 12.5 miles
  We add the initial quarter mile to get the maximum distance.
